text:
Very very good! Fast and easy too! First off, I NEVER use chicken breasts because I feel they are too dry, and lack flavor.  I ALWAYS substitute boneless skinless chicken thighs in all recipes that call for chicken. I trim off most excess fat from the thighs. I used fat free half and half for the heavy cream and then just thickened the sauce with a LITTLE cornstarch.  Also, I prepared extra sauce to pour over the pasta when served. I think the sauce is best made THE NIGHT BEFORE so the flavors can blend through(it's also easier that way if you're potlucking at work as we often do). Keep the sauce and pasta separate until serving or the pasta soaks up too much of the sauce. I agree with many about bumping up the Pesto.  I make my own Pesto so it packs plenty of flavor punch. Fast, easy and not fussy to make.  A hit with the crowd.

text:
Since I served this as a side dish with stuffed chicken, I omitted the chicken in this recipe. Wowie--I was blown away by this!  I always make my own pesto, as  I did this time, but this was the first time I've ever mixed it with cream and I was SO impressed that I probably will always make my pasta with pesto like this from now on. I also liked the fact that the recipe calls for a subtle amount of pesto and it was just right.  Too often I've experienced such a ton of pesto in dishes (restaurants, actually) that it is literally sickening. Not this time--and I think after this dish my husband has actually made friends with pesto!

This was very yummy!  I didn't have some key ingredients and took a risk and tried to make it a little different.  It was excellent and my husband absolutely loved it!  I didn't have heavy cream, butter or milk. I used just olive oil for cooking the chicken.  For the sauce I used jarred pesto, around 1/2-3/4 cup cream cheese, double amount of parmesan, a little mozzarella, and a 1/2 cup rice milk.  I was lucky and it turned out wonderful!!! I also added some broccoli to get our greens in there as well.

I made this exactly as the recipe states but I took the complaints of others into account.  Instead of doubling the sauce I made 1/2 more, and cut the penne down by removing one cup from the 16oz box.  I don't feel I had too much of one or the other and had enough sauce to soak up with a nice crusty bread.  The flavor was good, but I wish I would have thickened the sauce with maybe more cheese.  It was a little thin.  Would make again though.  When someone says not enough sauce I believe them.  A big Italian chain restaurant never gives enough sauce so I don't go there.  Who wants dry pasta...

I always chuckle when folks totally change a recipe and then say they loved it, but I am going to do it now.  I read a review that said to add sun-dried tomatoes, so I did.  Then I saw a pint of cherry tomatoes sitting in the fridge and decided to throw those in.  First, I cooked the cherry tomatoes separately with some oregano.  Once they had popped I mashed them and added them to the chicken.  Finally, I added the cream, actually fat free half-n-half, and the parmesan cheese.  We loved it.  Very tasty.  My husband told me to take the serving dish of pasta off the table before he ate it all!

text:
YUM YUM!  I made this tonight with some very garlic-y chicken strips I wanted to use.   I sauted the chicken strips with onions in butter.  I wanted more sauce, so I poured in 2 c cream(from the top of raw milk), and added about 1 c leftover peas and simmered them together.  I added a heaping 1/4 c of home made pesto I had frozen in ice cube trays this past summer and heated the whole thing through.  We mixed the sauce and chicken into 1  pound of penne right as we were ready to serve it.  This was a huge hit, very quick and easy, and I will likely serve it regularly.  Thanks MARYSTEVE!

text:
This is so yummy! Did substitute half and half for the cream and made my own pesto but you could easily use the pre-made stuff you buy at the grocery store. I have doubled and tripled the pesto before and its good with a little or a lot. I sauted 3 chicken breasts in the pan before making the sauce then set aside. Then in the same pan made a double batch of sauce, and then sauted for a few minutes while the pasta cooked. Then I mixed together the chicken and pasta into the sauce. Unless your going to decrease the amount of pasta used, then I would recommend doubling the sauce. This is so easy and delicious, I will be making again.       **one side note is that this dish is best finished on the night it is prepared because the leftovers cannot compare. The pasta absorbs all the yummy sauce and leave behind only olive oil.

This was simple and delicious. I changed things up a little bit. I added some Italian seasonings to the chicken while it cooked. After the chicken was cooked I removed it from the pan and added 1/4 cup white wine and 1/2 cup chicken broth and let it reduce. Then I added 1/2 cup pesto (instead of 1/4 cup the recipe called for) and the other ingredients. I added the chicken back when I put the pasta in. I also added some pasta water to help thicken the sauce. I used bow tie pasta because I didn't have penne. I will be making this again and perhaps trying the low fat substitutions suggested.

text:
Easy and delicious!  I sort of "eyeballed" the proportions to make it a bit saucier and pesto-heavy.  Cooked the pasta in one pot, sauted 2 chicken breasts (bite sized pieces) with chopped garlic and pepper in another, and 1 cup chicken broth, heavy cream and pesto warming in a saucepan.  Dumped them all together, added some parmesan cheese and mixed. Sprinkled grated Romano cheese and red pepper flakes on top before serving.  The red pepper flakes gave it a nice bit of pizazz!  Will definitely make again.

text:
This was a quick, simple, and delicious recipe.  My picky eaters compiled of my husband, five year old and three year old cleaned their plates.  I used frozen chicken tenders instead of breasts and cooked them through.  I removed them before making the sauce and returned them at the end.  As a footnote I usually always replace the heavy cream in a recipe with half and half to cut the fat.  Turns out beautifully.  Another mention is that I used a 14.5 oz box of pasta and only ended up using two thirds of it, otherwise sauce is scarce and I like sauce.  One last mention is that I probabaly ended up using 1/4c of freshly grated parmesan cheese, it needed more to thicken up the sauce.  None of these things changed the recipe, just personal preferences.  It was great, easy and delicious.

Delicious!!! But I did make some changes (I know, I know...giving a recipe 5* when you make changed, but they weren't drastic!) Okay: I made this w/o the chicken. So, if anyone else wants to try that, here's what I did. I used a 6.7 oz. jar of pesto (Spice World brand), which I mixed with the cream, olive oil, garlic, Parmesan cheese (used 5 T.), and a dash of grd. pepper. I cooked this until it was thick enough to be a sauce (which took about 15 minutes on medium). It was delicious, mixed with the penne pasta and had with the 'Soft Garlic Breadsticks' from this site & veggies. Wonderful! :)

Oh my God was this good!!!  I am from the south so I was not use to cooking with pesto and olive oil.  My 22 month old is so picky it is a miracle getting her to eat anything.  She actually ate some of it.  I read some of the reviews and added some things.  I didn't measure anything though I went based solely off of what I thought looked yummy.  I added flour so that the sauce would not be runny, I added sundried tomatoes, and lots of parmesan cheese.  It was delicious!  I will definantly make this one again.  I think that I will cook something other than Mac and Cheese, fried chicken, and tons of greese.  Of course I won't leave my soul food completely out!!  :)

text:
I ended up using 3 cloves of garlic with this dish and 1 cup of fat free half in half and 1/4 cup of chicken broth.  I added cornstarch to the half and half to obtain the thickness.  During the simmering I decided the sauce wasn't enough, so I doubled what was called for.  I added some shredded cheese and about a TB of sugar because with the added cheese and doubling of the sauce the dish was a bit too salty for my taste.  I immediately ate the food, but determined that my second helping was MUCH better than the first-during the time it set the flavors melted together more and gave such a stronger flavor.  Overall, it was a good dish and I'll make it again.

I also added a package of sliced baby portabello mushrooms and doubled the amount of pesto and tripled the garlic. I made homemade pesto from my basil this summer, and proceeded to look for recipes to use it in.  This was a very good, fast, and easy dish to make.  I only gave it 4 stars, however, because mine was a bit bland and dry until I added extra pesto and more liquid.  Afterward, though, it was very delicious.  I agree with other reviewers that using chicken broth in place of some of the cream would be a good idea for less fat and as well as extra flavor.  I'll try it next time.

text:
Excellent base recipe! I made this dish with just a few modifications and it was so delicious. I used Perdue frozen chicken strips instead of chicken breast. I marinated the strips in a garlic-based marinade overnight. The next morning, I made the sauce. I substituted Classico Four Cheese Alfredo sauce for the heavy cream and added diced Mezzetta Sun-Ripened Dried Tomatoes for colors. I let the sauce "sit" for several hours to let the flavors go through. I also added twice the pesto called for in the recipe because I love pesto and added garlic powder/red pepper flakes for additional seasoning. By the time, I prepared the penne, the sauce had thickened nicely and the flavor was superb! Thanks for this awesome recipe!

text:
I've made this so many times that I don't even need the recipe anymore. A few changes I make:

1- I use a full cup of pesto sauce. (We love pesto- the more flavor, the better.)
2- I add a tablespoon of flour to the sauce to help thicken it. It takes approximately 15-20 minutes of stirring over low heat to get the consistency we like, but it's worth it.
3- Sometimes I cheat and use the pre-cooked and pre-sliced chicken breast meat.

This also reheats well for leftovers. I admit it's not the healthiest recipe, but it's certainly a delicious one!
